      <p><b>Haiti</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'h' in 'hi'">h</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Haiti.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/En-us-Haiti.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Haiti.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Haïti</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[a.iti]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Haitian Creole language">Haitian Creole</a>: <i lang="ht">Ayiti</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Haitian_Creole" title="Help:IPA/Haitian Creole">[ajiti]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Haiti</b> (French: <i lang="fr">République d'Haïti</i>; Haitian Creole: <i lang="ht">Repiblik d Ayiti</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and formerly known as <b>Hayti</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[note 1]</a></sup> is a country located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> archipelago of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, to the east of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>. It occupies the western three-eighths of the island which it shares with the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dardik_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dardik-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Current_Affairs_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Current_Affairs-19">[18]</a></sup> To its south-west lies the small island of <a href="/wiki/Navassa_Island" title="Navassa Island">Navassa Island</a>, which is claimed by Haiti but is disputed as a <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands" title="United States Minor Outlying Islands">territory</a> under federal administration.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_Haiti_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_Haiti-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Haiti is 27,750 square kilometers (10,714&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in size, the third largest country in the Caribbean by area, and has an estimated population of 11.4 million<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-7">[7]</a></sup>, making it the most populous country in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. </p>
      <p>The island was originally inhabited by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> people, who migrated from South America.<sup id="cite_ref-national-geographic_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-national-geographic-22">[21]</a></sup> The first Europeans arrived on 5 December 1492 during the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus#First_voyage" title="Christopher Columbus">first voyage</a> of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, who initially believed he had found <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> or <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NgCheong-Lum,_Roseline_19_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NgCheong-Lum,_Roseline_19-23">[22]</a></sup> Columbus subsequently founded the first European settlement in the Americas, <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a>, on what is now the northeastern coast of Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies1953_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies1953-24">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> The island was claimed by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> and named <i>La Española,</i> forming part of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> until the early 17th century. However, competing claims and settlements by the French led to the western portion of the island being <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Ryswick" title="Peace of Ryswick">ceded to France</a> in 1697, which was subsequently named <i>Saint-Domingue</i>. French colonists established lucrative <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">plantations</a>, worked by vast numbers of slaves brought from Africa, which made the colony one of the richest in the world. </p>
      <p>In the midst of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> (1789–99), slaves and <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> launched the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> (1791–1804), led by a former slave and the first black general of the <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a>. After 12 years of conflict, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> Bonaparte's forces were defeated by Louverture's successor, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a> (later Emperor Jacques I), who declared Haiti's sovereignty on 1 January 1804—the first independent <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, the second <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> in the Americas, the first country to abolish slavery, and the only state in history established by a successful <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave revolt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Apart from <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, the first President of the Republic, all of Haiti's first leaders were former slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> After a brief period in which the country was split in two, President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">Jean-Pierre Boyer</a> united the country and then attempted to bring the whole of Hispaniola under Haitian control, precipitating a long series of wars that ended in the 1870s when Haiti formally recognized the independence of the Dominican Republic. Haiti's first century of independence was characterized by political instability, ostracism by the international community and the payment of a crippling debt to France. Political volatility and foreign economic influence in the country prompted the U.S. to occupy the country from 1915 to 1934. Following a series of short-lived presidencies, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duvalier" title="François Duvalier">François 'Papa Doc' Duvalier</a> took power in 1956, ushering in a long period of autocratic rule that was continued by his son <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">Jean-Claude 'Baby Doc' Duvalier</a> that lasted until 1986; the period was characterized by state-sanctioned violence against the opposition and civilians, corruption, and economic stagnation. Since 1986 Haiti has been attempting to establish a more democratic political system. </p>
      <p>Haiti is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS),<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">International Francophonie Organisation</a>. In addition to <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a>, it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a>. Historically poor and politically unstable, Haiti has the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> in the Americas. Since the turn of the 21st century, the country has endured a <i><a href="/wiki/2004_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2004 Haitian coup d'état">coup d'état</a>,</i> which prompted a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilisation_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilisation Mission in Haiti">U.N. intervention</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">a deadly earthquake</a> that killed over 250,000. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <p>The name Haiti (or <i>Hayti</i>) comes from the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> language which was the native name<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[note 2]</a></sup> given to the entire island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> to mean, "land of high mountains."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> The <i>h</i> is silent in French and the <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%8F" title="Ï">ï</a></i> in <i>Ha<b>ï</b>ti</i> has a <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)#French" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">diacritical mark</a> used to show that the second vowel is pronounced separately, as in the word <i>na<b>ï</b>ve</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> In English, this rule for the pronunciation is often disregarded, thus the spelling <i>Haiti</i> is used. There are different anglicizations for its pronunciation such as <i>HIGH-ti</i>, <i>high-EE-ti</i> and <i>haa-EE-ti</i>, which are still in use, but <i>HAY-ti</i> is the most widespread and best-established.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> The name was restored by Haitian revolutionary Jean-Jacques Dessalines as the official name of independent Saint-Domingue, as a tribute to the Amerindian predecessors.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In French, Haiti's nickname is the "Pearl of the Antilles" (<i>La Perle des Antilles</i>) because of both its natural beauty,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> and the amount of wealth it accumulated for the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a>; during the 18th century the colony was the world's leading producer of sugar and coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Haiti" title="History of Haiti">History of Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_history">Pre-Columbian history</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chiefdoms_of_Hispaniola" title="Chiefdoms of Hispaniola">Chiefdoms of Hispaniola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/350px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/525px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/700px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 2x" data-file-width="2341" data-file-height="1171"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The five <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">caciquedoms</a> of Hispaniola at the time of the arrival of Christopher Columbus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, of which Haiti occupies the western three-eighths,<sup id="cite_ref-Dardik_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dardik-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Current_Affairs_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Current_Affairs-19">[18]</a></sup> has been inhabited since about 5000 BC by groups of Native Americans thought to have arrived from Central or South America.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Genetic studies show that some of these groups were related to the <a href="/wiki/Yanomami" title="Yanomami">Yanomami</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-national-geographic_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-national-geographic-22">[21]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> Amongst these early settlers were the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a> peoples, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taíno people">Taíno</a>, speakers of an <a href="/wiki/Arawakan" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawakan">Arawakan</a> <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Taíno language">language</a>, elements of which have been preserved in <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>. The Taíno name for the entire island was <i>Haiti</i>, or alternatively <i>Quisqeya</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt9_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt9-46">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Taíno society the largest unit of political organization was led by a <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a>,</i> or chief, as the Europeans understood them. The island of Hipaniola was divided among five 'caciquedoms': the Magua in the north east, the Marien in the north west, the Jaragua in the south west, the Maguana in the central regions of Cibao, and the Higüey in the south east.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Taíno cultural artifacts include <a href="/wiki/Cave_paintings" class="mw-redirect" title="Cave paintings">cave paintings</a> in several locations in the country. These have become national symbols of Haiti and tourist attractions. Modern-day <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9og%C3%A2ne" title="Léogâne">Léogâne</a>, started as a French colonial town in the southwest, is beside the former capital of the caciquedom of <i>Xaragua.</i><sup id="cite_ref-royal_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal-49">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Spanish_rule_.281492.E2.80.931625.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_rule_(1492–1625)">Spanish rule (1492–1625)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Viceroyalty" title="Columbian Viceroyalty">Columbian Viceroyalty</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Captaincy General of Santo Domingo">Captaincy General of Santo Domingo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/220px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/330px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/440px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg 2x" data-file-width="816" data-file-height="693"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Christopher Columbus landing on Hispaniola
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Piktograf1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Piktograf1.png/220px-Piktograf1.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Piktograf1.png/330px-Piktograf1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Piktograf1.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Piktograf1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1510 Taíno <a href="/wiki/Pictograph" class="mw-redirect" title="Pictograph">pictograph</a> telling a story of missionaries arriving in <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Navigator <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> landed in Haiti on 6 December 1492, in an area that he named <i><a href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le-Saint-Nicolas" title="Môle-Saint-Nicolas">Môle-Saint-Nicolas</a>,</i><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> and claimed the island for the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>. Nineteen days later, his ship the <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">Santa María</a></i> ran aground near the present site of <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>. Columbus left 39 men on the island, who founded the settlement of <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a> on 25 December 1492.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Relations with the native peoples, initially good, broke down and the settlers were later killed by the Taíno.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt10_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt10-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The sailors carried endemic Eurasian <a href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a> to which the native peoples lacked <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a>, causing them to die in great numbers in <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> The first recorded <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> epidemic in the Americas erupted on Hispaniola in 1507.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Their numbers were further reduced by the harshness of the <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a></i></i> system, in which the Spanish forced natives to work in gold mines and plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt10_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt10-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Spanish passed the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Burgos" title="Laws of Burgos">Laws of Burgos, 1512–13</a>, which forbade the maltreatment of natives, endorsed their <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">conversion</a> to Catholicism,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> and gave legal framework to <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">encomiendas</i>.</i> The natives were brought to these sites to work in specific plantations or industries.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As the Spanish re-focused their colonization efforts on the greater riches of mainland Central and South America, Hispaniola became reduced largely to a trading and refueling post. As a result <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">piracy</a> became widespread, encouraged by European powers hostile to Spain such as France (based on <a href="/wiki/Tortuga_(Haiti)" title="Tortuga (Haiti)">Île de la Tortue</a>) and England.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt10_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt10-51">[49]</a></sup> The Spanish largely abandoned the western third of the island, focusing their colonization effort on the eastern two-thirds.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> The western part of the island was thus gradually settled by French <a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">buccaneers</a>; among them was Bertrand d'Ogeron, who succeeded in growing <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> and recruited many French colonial families from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> In 1697 <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Spain">Spain</a> settled their hostilities on the island by way of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ryswick" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Ryswick">Treaty of Ryswick</a> of 1697, which divided Hispaniola between them.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="French_rule_.281625.E2.80.931804.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_rule_(1625–1804)">French rule (1625–1804)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <p>France received the western third and subsequently named it <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, the French equivalent of <i><a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Captaincy General of Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a></i>, the Spanish colony on <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-firstcolony_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstcolony-61">[59]</a></sup> The French set about creating sugar and coffee plantations, worked by vast numbers of slaves imported from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and Saint-Domingue grew to become their richest colonial possession.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French settlers were outnumbered by slaves by almost 10 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> According to the 1788 Census, Haiti's population consisted of nearly 25,000 Europeans, 22,000 free coloreds and 700,000 African slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> In contrast, by 1763 the white population of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">French Canada</a>, a far larger territory, had numbered only 65,000.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> In the north of the island, slaves were able to retain many ties to African cultures, religion and language; these ties were continually being renewed by newly imported Africans. Some West African slaves held on to their traditional <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Vodou</a> beliefs by secretly syncretizing it with Catholicism.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French enacted the <i><a href="/wiki/Code_Noir" title="Code Noir">Code Noir</a></i> ("Black Code"), prepared by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Colbert" title="Jean-Baptiste Colbert">Jean-Baptiste Colbert</a> and ratified by <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, which established rules on slave treatment and permissible freedoms.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt12_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt12-64">[62]</a></sup> Saint-Domingue has been described as one of the most brutally efficient slave colonies; one-third of newly imported Africans died within a few years.<sup id="cite_ref-Farmer-LROB_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer-LROB-65">[63]</a></sup> Many slaves died from diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> They had low <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> and there is evidence that some women <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">aborted</a> fetuses rather than give birth to children within the bonds of slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> The colony's environment also suffered, as forests were cleared to make way for plantations and the land was overworked so as to extract maximum profit for French plantation owners.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791,_German_copper_engraving.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg/220px-Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg/330px-Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg/440px-Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791%2C_German_copper_engraving.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="511"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fire_in_Saint-Domingo_1791,_German_copper_engraving.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Saint-Domingue <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave revolt</a> in 1791
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As in its <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana colony</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">French colonial</a> government allowed some rights to <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> (<i>gens de couleur</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Mixed-race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> descendants of European male colonists and African female slaves (and later, mixed-race women).<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> Over time, many were released from slavery and they established a separate <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social class</a>. White French <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a> fathers frequently sent their mixed-race sons to <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> for their education. Some men of color were admitted into the military. More of the free people of color lived in the south of the island, near <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, and many intermarried within their community.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> They frequently worked as artisans and tradesmen, and began to own some property, including slaves of their own.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> The free people of color petitioned the <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">colonial</a> government to expand their rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The brutality of slave life led many slaves to escape to mountainous regions, where they set up their own autonomous communities and became known as <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> One Maroon leader, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mackandal" title="François Mackandal">François Mackandal</a>, led a rebellion in the 1750s, however he was later captured and executed by the French.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt11_60-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt11-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Haitian_Revolution_.281791.E2.80.931804.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Haitian_Revolution_(1791–1804)">Haitian Revolution (1791–1804)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif/220px-Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif/330px-Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif/440px-Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="494"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Haitian_Revolution_-_Blacks_murdering_white_civilians.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_massacre#The_Haitian_Revolution" title="1804 Haiti massacre">Black slaves</a> murdering French settlers in a massacre that effectively eliminated the white population of Haiti
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/220px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/330px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/440px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg 2x" data-file-width="457" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>General <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> of 1789 and principles of the <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_man" class="mw-redirect" title="Rights of man">rights of man</a>, the French settlers and free people of color pressed for greater political freedom and more <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt12_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt12-64">[62]</a></sup> Tensions between these two groups led to conflict, as a militia of free-coloreds was set up in 1790 by <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Og%C3%A9" title="Vincent Ogé">Vincent Ogé</a>, resulting in his capture, torture and execution.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Sensing an opportunity, in August 1791 the first slave armies were established in northern Haiti under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a> inspired by the Vodou <i>houngan</i> (priest) Boukman, and backed by the Spanish in Santo Domingo – soon a full-blown slave rebellion had broken out across the entire colony.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1792, the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French</a> government sent three commissioners with troops to re-establish control; to build an alliance with the <i><a href="/wiki/Gens_de_couleur" class="mw-redirect" title="Gens de couleur">gens de couleur</a></i> and slaves commissioners <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9ger-F%C3%A9licit%C3%A9_Sonthonax" title="Léger-Félicité Sonthonax">Léger-Félicité Sonthonax</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Polverel" title="Étienne Polverel">Étienne Polverel</a> abolished slavery in the colony.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt12_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt12-64">[62]</a></sup> Six months later, the <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Maximilien_de_Robespierre" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximilien de Robespierre">Maximilien de Robespierre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jacobin_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobin Club">Jacobins</a>, endorsed <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">abolition</a> and extended it to all the French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Political leaders in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, which was a new republic itself, reacted with ambivalence, at times providing aid to enable <a href="/wiki/Planter_(plantation_owner)" class="mw-redirect" title="Planter (plantation owner)">planters</a> to put down the revolt. Later in the revolution, the US provided support to native Haitian military forces, with the goal of reducing French influence in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With slavery abolished, Toussaint Louverture pledged allegiance to France, and he fought off the British and Spanish forces who had taken advantage of the situation and invaded Saint-Domingue.<sup id="cite_ref-Latin_America's_Wars:_Volume_1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_America's_Wars:_Volume_1-72">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> The Spanish were later forced to cede their part of the island to France under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Basel" title="Peace of Basel">Peace of Basel</a> in 1795, uniting the island under one government. However an insurgency against French rule broke out in the east, and in the west there was fighting between Louverture's forces and the free people of color led by <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rigaud" title="André Rigaud">André Rigaud</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Knives" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Knives">War of the Knives</a> (1799–1800).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> Many surviving free people of color left the island as refugees.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/220px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/330px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/440px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="642"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Battle between <a href="/wiki/Polish_Legions_(Napoleonic_period)" title="Polish Legions (Napoleonic period)">Polish troops</a> in French service and the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian rebels</a>. The majority of Polish soldiers eventually deserted the French army and fought alongside the Haitians.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Louverture created a separatist constitution and proclaimed himself governor-general for life, <a href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoléon Bonaparte">Napoléon Bonaparte</a> in 1802 sent an expedition of 20,000 soldiers and as many sailors<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> under the command of his brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc_(general,_born_1772)" title="Charles Leclerc (general, born 1772)">Charles Leclerc</a>, to reassert French control. The French achieved some victories, but within a few months most of their <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">army</a> had died from <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> Ultimately more than 50,000 French troops died in an attempt to retake the colony, including 18 generals.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> The French managed to capture Louverture, transporting him to France for trial. He was imprisoned at <a href="/wiki/Fort_de_Joux" title="Fort de Joux">Fort de Joux</a>, where he died in 1803 of exposure and possibly <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Farmer-LROB_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer-LROB-65">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The slaves, along with free <i>gens de couleur</i> and allies, continued their fight for independence, led by generals <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Christophe" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Christophe">Henry Christophe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> The rebels finally managed to decisively defeat the French troops at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verti%C3%A8res" title="Battle of Vertières">Battle of Vertières</a> on 18 November 1803, leading the first ever nation to successfully gain independence through a slave revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Under the overall command of Dessalines, the Haitian armies avoided open battle, and instead conducted a successful guerrilla campaign against the Napoleonic forces, working with diseases such as yellow fever to reduce the numbers of French soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> Later that year France withdrew its remaining 7,000 troops from the island and Napoleon gave up his idea of re-establishing a <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> empire, selling <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana (New France)</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> It has been estimated that between 24,000 and 100,000 Europeans, and between 100,000 and 350,000 Haitian ex-slaves, died in the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> In the process, Dessalines became arguably the most successful military commander in the struggle against Napoleonic France.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Haiti">Independent Haiti</span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="First_Empire_.281804.E2.80.931806.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Empire_(1804–1806)">First Empire (1804–1806)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Empire_of_Haiti" title="First Empire of Haiti">First Empire of Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="1804 Haiti Massacre">1804 Haiti Massacre</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres,_1823.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg/220px-Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg/330px-Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg/440px-Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres%2C_1823.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1328" data-file-height="1950"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Le_Serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres,_1823.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pétion and Dessalines swearing allegiance to each other before God; painting by <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Guillon-Lethi%C3%A8re" title="Guillaume Guillon-Lethière">Guillon-Lethière</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The independence of Saint-Domingue was proclaimed under the native name 'Haiti' by Dessalines on 1 January 1804 in <a href="/wiki/Gona%C3%AFves" title="Gonaïves">Gonaïves</a><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-84">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt209_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt209-85">[83]</a></sup> and he was proclaimed "Emperor for Life" as Emperor Jacques I by his troops.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Dessalines at first offered protection to the white planters and others.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> However, once in power, he ordered the <a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="1804 Haiti Massacre">massacre</a> of nearly all white men, women, children; between January and April 1804, 3,000 to 5,000 whites were killed, including those who had been friendly and sympathetic to the black population.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies2008_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2008-88">[86]</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_massacre#Aftermath" title="1804 Haiti massacre">three categories of white people</a> were selected out as exceptions and spared: <a href="/wiki/Polish_Haitian" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Haitian">Polish</a> soldiers, the majority of whom had deserted from the French army and fought alongside the Haitian rebels; the small group of <a href="/wiki/German_Haitian" class="mw-redirect" title="German Haitian">German</a> colonists invited to the <a href="/wiki/Nord-Ouest_(department)" title="Nord-Ouest (department)">north-west region</a>; and a group of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">medical doctors</a> and professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Reportedly, people with connections to officers in the Haitian army were also spared, as well as the women who agreed to marry non-white men.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fearful of the potential impact the slave rebellion could have in the <a href="/wiki/Slave_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave states">slave states</a>, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> refused to recognize the new republic. The Southern politicians who were a powerful voting bloc in the American Congress prevented U.S. recognition for decades until they withdrew in 1861 to form the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The revolution led to a wave of emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> In 1809, 9,000 refugees from Saint-Domingue, both white planters and people of color, settled <i>en masse</i> in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, doubling the city's population, having been expelled from their initial refuge in Cuba by Spanish authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> In addition, the newly arrived slaves added to the city's African population.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The plantation system was reestablished in Haiti, albeit for wages, however many Haitians were marginalized and resented the heavy-handed manner in which this was enforced in the new nation's politics.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> The rebel movement splintered, and Dessalines was assassinated by rivals on 17 October 1806.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiti_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti-95">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="State_of_Haiti.2C_Kingdom_of_Haiti_and_the_Republic_.281806.E2.80.931820.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Haiti,_Kingdom_of_Haiti_and_the_Republic_(1806–1820)">State of Haiti, Kingdom of Haiti and the Republic (1806–1820)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/State_of_Haiti" title="State of Haiti">State of Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Haiti" title="Kingdom of Haiti">Kingdom of Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/220px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/330px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/440px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3022" data-file-height="2015"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Citadelle Laferrière">Citadelle Laferrière</a>, built 1805–22, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Fortress" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortress">fortress</a> in the Americas, and is considered locally to be the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_wonder_of_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth wonder of the world">eighth wonder of the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reading_Eagle_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reading_Eagle-96">[94]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Dessalines' death Haiti became split into two, with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Haiti" title="Kingdom of Haiti">Kingdom of Haiti</a> in the north directed by Henri Christophe, later declaring himself <a href="/wiki/Henri_Christophe" title="Henri Christophe">Henri I</a>, and a republic in the south centred on Port-au-Prince, directed by <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, an <i>homme de couleur</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> Christophe established a semi-feudal <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corvée">corvée</a> system, with a rigid education and economic code.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> Pétion's republic was less absolutist, and he initiated a series of land reforms which benefited the peasant class.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt13_79-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt13-79">[77]</a></sup> President Pétion also gave military and financial assistance to the revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, which were critical in enabling him to liberate the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> Meanwhile the French, who had managed to maintain a precarious control of eastern Hispaniola, were <a href="/wiki/Spanish_reconquest_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Spanish reconquest of Santo Domingo">defeated</a> by insurgents led by <a href="/wiki/Juan_S%C3%A1nchez_Ram%C3%ADrez" title="Juan Sánchez Ramírez">Juan Sánchez Ramírez</a>, with the area returning to Spanish rule in 1809 following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Hincado" title="Battle of Palo Hincado">Battle of Palo Hincado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RECONQUEST_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RECONQUEST-103">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Unification_of_Hispaniola_.281821.E2.80.931844.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Unification_of_Hispaniola_(1821–1844)">Unification of Hispaniola (1821–1844)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Haiti_(1820%E2%80%931849)" title="Republic of Haiti (1820–1849)">Republic of Haiti (1820–1849)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Hispaniola" title="Unification of Hispaniola">Unification of Hispaniola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/220px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/330px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/440px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="560"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">Jean-Pierre Boyer</a>, ruler of Haiti 1818–1843
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Beginning in 1821, President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">Jean-Pierre Boyer</a>, also an <i>homme de couleur</i> and successor to Pétion, reunified the island following the suicide of Henry Christophe.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Spanish_Haiti" title="Republic of Spanish Haiti">Santo Domingo</a> declared its independence from Spain on 30 November 1821, Boyer invaded, seeking to <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Hispaniola" title="Unification of Hispaniola">unite the entire island</a> by force and ending slavery in Santo Domingo.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Struggling to revive the agricultural economy to produce <a href="/wiki/Commodity_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Commodity crops">commodity crops</a>, Boyer passed the Code Rural, which denied peasant laborers the right to leave the land, enter the towns, or start farms or shops of their own, causing much resentment as most peasants wished to have their own farms rather than work on plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a> (ACS) encouraged <a href="/wiki/Free_negro" class="mw-redirect" title="Free negro">free blacks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> to emigrate to Haiti. Starting in September 1824, more than 6,000 <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a> migrated to Haiti, with transportation paid by the ACS.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> Many found the conditions too harsh and returned to the United States. </p>
      <p>In July 1825, <a href="/wiki/Charles_X" title="Charles X">King Charles X</a> of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, during a period of restoration of the <a href="/wiki/French_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="French monarchy">French monarchy</a>, sent a <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">fleet</a> to reconquer Haiti. Under pressure, President Boyer agreed to a treaty by which France formally recognized the independence of the nation in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Haiti_indemnity_controversy" title="Haiti indemnity controversy">a payment</a> of 150 million <a href="/wiki/Francs" class="mw-redirect" title="Francs">francs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> By an order of 17 April 1826, the King of France renounced his rights of sovereignty and formally recognized the independence of Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-FrenchEmbassy_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FrenchEmbassy-109">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> The enforced payments to France hampered Haiti's economic growth for years, exacerbated by the fact that many Western nations continued to refuse formal <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic</a> recognition to Haiti; Britain recognized Haitian independence in 1833, and the United States not until 1862.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Haiti borrowed heavily from Western banks at extremely high interest rates to repay the debt. Although the amount of the reparations was reduced to 90 million in 1838, by 1900 80% of the country's gross domestic product was being spent on debt repayment<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> and the country did not finish repaying it until 1947.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_the_Spanish_portion_of_the_island">Loss of the Spanish portion of the island</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dominican_War_of_Independence" title="Dominican War of Independence">Dominican War of Independence</a>
      </div> 
      <p>After losing the support of Haiti's elite, Boyer was ousted in 1843, with <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rivi%C3%A8re-H%C3%A9rard" title="Charles Rivière-Hérard">Charles Rivière-Hérard</a> replacing him as president.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> Nationalist Dominican forces in eastern Hispaniola led by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Duarte" title="Juan Pablo Duarte">Juan Pablo Duarte</a> seized control of Santo Domingo on 27 February 1844.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> The Haitian forces, unprepared for a significant uprising, capitulated to the rebels, effectively ending Haitian rule of eastern Hispaniola. In March Rivière-Hérard attempted to reimpose his authority, but the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominicans</a> put up stiff opposition and inflicted heavy losses.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> Rivière-Hérard was removed from office by the mulatto hierarchy and replaced with the aged general <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Guerrier" title="Philippe Guerrier">Philippe Guerrier</a>, who assumed the presidency on 3 May 1844. </p>
      <p>Guerrier died in April 1845, and was succeeded by General <a href="/wiki/Jean-Louis_Pierrot" title="Jean-Louis Pierrot">Jean-Louis Pierrot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-leger197_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leger197-115">[113]</a></sup> Pierrot's most pressing duty as the new president was to check the incursions of the Dominicans, who were harassing the Haitian troops.<sup id="cite_ref-leger197_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leger197-115">[113]</a></sup> Dominican gunboats were also making depredations on Haiti's coasts.<sup id="cite_ref-leger197_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leger197-115">[113]</a></sup> President Pierrot decided to open a campaign against the Dominicans, whom he considered merely as insurgents, however the Haitian offensive of 1845 was stopped on the frontier.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 January 1846 Pierrot announced a fresh campaign to re-imposed Haitian suzerainty over eastern Hispaniola, but his officers and men greeted this fresh summons with contempt.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> Thus, a month later – February 1846 – when Pierrot ordered his troops to march against the Dominicans, the Haitian army mutinied, and its soldiers proclaimed his overthrow as president of the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> With the war against the Dominicans having become very unpopular in Haiti, it was beyond the power of the new president, General <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Rich%C3%A9" title="Jean-Baptiste Riché">Jean-Baptiste Riché</a>, to stage another invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Second_Empire_.281849.E2.80.931859.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Empire_(1849–1859)">Second Empire (1849–1859)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_of_Haiti" title="Second Empire of Haiti">Second Empire of Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Faustin_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faustin_I.jpg/220px-Faustin_I.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="345" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faustin_I.jpg/330px-Faustin_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Faustin_I.jpg/440px-Faustin_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="485" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Faustin_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Faustin I, from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Illustrated_London_News" title="The Illustrated London News">The Illustrated London News</a></i>, 16 February 1856
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 27 February 1847, President Riché died after only a year in power and was replaced by an obscure officer, General <a href="/wiki/Faustin_Soulouque" title="Faustin Soulouque">Faustin Soulouque</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> During the first two years of Soulouque's administration the conspiracies and opposition he faced in retaining power were so manifold that the Dominicans were given a further breathing space in which to consolidate their independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> But, when in 1848 France finally recognized the Dominican Republic as a free and independent state and provisionally signed a treaty of peace, friendship, commerce and navigation, Haiti immediately protested, claiming the treaty was an attack upon their own security.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> Soulouque decided to invade the new Republic before the French Government could ratify the treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-Bethell_114-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bethell-114">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 21 March 1849, Haitian soldiers attacked the Dominican garrison at <a href="/wiki/Las_Matas_de_Farf%C3%A1n" title="Las Matas de Farfán">Las Matas</a>. The demoralized defenders offered almost no resistance before abandoning their weapons. Soulouque pressed on, capturing <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Province_(Dominican_Republic)" title="San Juan Province (Dominican Republic)">San Juan</a>. This left only the town of <a href="/wiki/Azua,_Dominican_Republic" title="Azua, Dominican Republic">Azua</a> as the remaining Dominican stronghold between the Haitian army and the capital. On 6 April, Azua fell to the 18,000-strong Haitian army, with a 5,000-man Dominican counterattack failing to oust them.<sup id="cite_ref-Latin_America's_Wars:_Volume_1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latin_America's_Wars:_Volume_1-72">[70]</a></sup> The way to <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> was now clear. But the news of discontent existing at Port-au-Prince, which reached Soulouque, arrested his further progress and caused him to return with the army to his capital.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Emboldened by the sudden retreat of the Haitian army, the Dominicans counter-attacked. Their flotilla went as far as <a href="/wiki/Dame-Marie,_Grand%27Anse" title="Dame-Marie, Grand'Anse">Dame-Marie</a>, which they plundered and set on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> Soulouque, now self-proclaimed as Emperor Faustin I, decided to start a new campaign against them. In 1855, he again invaded the territory of the Dominican Republic. But owing to insufficient preparation, the army was soon in want of victuals and ammunition.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> In spite of the bravery of the soldiers, the Emperor had once more to give up the idea of a unified island under Haitian control.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> After this campaign, Britain and France interfered and obtained an armistice on behalf of the Dominicans, who declared independence as the Dominican Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The sufferings endured by the soldiers during the campaign of 1855, and the losses and sacrifices inflicted on the country without yielding any compensation or any practical results provoked great discontent.<sup id="cite_ref-Jacques_116-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacques-116">[114]</a></sup> In 1858 a revolution began, led by General <a href="/wiki/Fabre_Geffrard" title="Fabre Geffrard">Fabre Geffrard</a>, Duke of Tabara. In December of that year, Geffrard defeated the Imperial Army and seized control of most of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti_21-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encylopedia_Britannica_-_Haiti-21">[20]</a></sup> As a result, the Emperor abdicated his throne on 15 January 1859. Refused aid by the French Legation, Faustin was taken into exile aboard a British warship on 22 January 1859, and General Geffrard succeeded him as President. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Late_19th_century.E2.80.93early_20th_century"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_19th_century–early_20th_century">Late 19th century–early 20th century</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Luders_Affair,_Germany,_Haiti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/220px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/330px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/440px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="882" data-file-height="586"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Luders_Affair,_Germany,_Haiti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>German Captain Thiele of the <i>Charlotte</i> handing over the German Ultimatum on 6 December 1897 during the Lüders Affair
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The period following Soulouque's overthrow down to the turn of the century was a turbulent one for Haiti, with repeated bouts of political instability. President Geffrard was overthrown in a coup in 1867,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> as was his successor, <a href="/wiki/Sylvain_Salnave" title="Sylvain Salnave">Sylvain Salnave</a>, in 1869.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> Under the Presidency of <a href="/wiki/Michel_Domingue" title="Michel Domingue">Michel Domingue</a> (1874–76) relations with the Dominican Republic were dramatically improved by the signing of a treaty, in which both parties acknowledged the independence of the other, bringing an end to Haitian dreams of bringing the entirety of Hispaniola under their control. Some modernisation of the economy and infrastructure also occurred in this period, especially under the Presidencies of <a href="/wiki/Lysius_Salomon" title="Lysius Salomon">Lysius Salomon</a> (1879–88) and <a href="/wiki/Florvil_Hyppolite" title="Florvil Hyppolite">Florvil Hyppolite</a> (1889–96).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Haiti's relations with outside powers were often strained. In 1889 the United States attempted to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le_Saint-Nicolas_affair" title="Môle Saint-Nicolas affair">force Haiti</a> to permit the building of a naval base at <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le_Saint-Nicolas" class="mw-redirect" title="Môle Saint-Nicolas">Môle Saint-Nicolas</a>, which was firmly resisted by President Hyppolite.<sup id="cite_ref-leger245_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leger245-120">[118]</a></sup> In 1892 the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German government</a> supported suppression of the reform movement of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%A9nor_Firmin" title="Anténor Firmin">Anténor Firmin</a>, and in 1897, the Germans used <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">gunboat diplomacy</a> to intimidate and then humiliate the Haitian government of President <a href="/wiki/Tir%C3%A9sias_Simon_Sam" title="Tirésias Simon Sam">Tirésias Simon Sam</a> (1896–1902) during the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCders_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Lüders Affair">Lüders Affair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first decades of the 20th century, Haiti experienced great political instability and was heavily in debt to France, Germany and the United States. A series of short lived presidencies came and went: President <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Nord_Alexis" title="Pierre Nord Alexis">Pierre Nord Alexis</a> was forced from power in 1908,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> as was his successor <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_C._Antoine_Simon" title="François C. Antoine Simon">François C. Antoine Simon</a> in 1911;<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Cincinnatus_Leconte" title="Cincinnatus Leconte">Cincinnatus Leconte</a> (1911–12) was killed in a (possibly deliberate) explosion at the National Palace;<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michel_Oreste" title="Michel Oreste">Michel Oreste</a> (1913–14) was ousted in a coup, as was his successor <a href="/wiki/Oreste_Zamor" title="Oreste Zamor">Oreste Zamor</a> in 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="United_States_occupation_.281915.E2.80.931934.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_occupation_(1915–1934)">United States occupation (1915–1934)</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Haiti" title="United States occupation of Haiti">United States occupation of Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti,_circa_1919.,_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-220px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-330px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-440px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2599"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti,_circa_1919.,_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>U.S. Marines and guide in search of Haitian <a href="/wiki/Cacos_(military_group)" title="Cacos (military group)">Cacos</a> fighters against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Haiti" title="United States occupation of Haiti">U.S. occupation of Haiti</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">  1919</span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
