      <p>Haiti has a rich and unique cultural identity, consisting of a blend of traditional French and African customs, mixed with sizeable contributions from the Spanish and indigenous Taíno cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-Yurnet-Thomas_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yurnet-Thomas-355">[353]</a></sup> Haiti's culture is greatly reflected in its paintings, music, and literature. Galleries and museums in the United States and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> have exhibited the works of the better-known artists to have come out of Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-Haitians_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haitians-356">[354]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_art" title="Haitian art">Haitian art</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Haitian art is <a href="/wiki/Haitian_art" title="Haitian art">distinctive</a>, particularly through its paintings and sculptures.<sup id="cite_ref-Yurnet-Thomas_355-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yurnet-Thomas-355">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[355]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[356]</a></sup> Brilliant colors, <a href="/wiki/Na%C3%AFve_art" title="Naïve art">naïve</a> perspectives, and sly humor characterize <a href="/wiki/Haitian_art" title="Haitian art">Haitian art</a>. Frequent subjects in Haitian art include big, delectable foods, lush landscapes, market activities, jungle animals, rituals, dances, and gods. As a result of a deep history and strong African ties, symbols take on great meaning within Haitian society. For example, a rooster often represents Aristide and the red and blue colors of the Haitian flag often represent his Lavalas party.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many artists cluster in 'schools' of painting, such as the Cap-Haïtien school, which features depictions of daily life in the city, the Jacmel School, which reflects the steep mountains and bays of that coastal town, or the Saint-Soleil School, which is characterised by abstracted human forms and is heavily influenced by Vodou symbolism.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1920s the <i>indigéniste</i> movement gained international acclaim, with its expressionist paintings inspired by Haiti's culture and African roots. Notable painters of this movement include <a href="/wiki/Hector_Hyppolite" title="Hector Hyppolite">Hector Hyppolite</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Philom%C3%A9_Oban&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Philomé Oban (page does not exist)">Philomé Oban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A9f%C3%A8te_Duffaut" title="Préfète Duffaut">Préfète Duffaut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt36_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt36-359">[357]</a></sup> Some notable artists of more recent times include <a href="/wiki/Edouard_Duval-Carri%C3%A9" title="Edouard Duval-Carrié">Edouard Duval-Carrié</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Frantz_Z%C3%A9phirin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Frantz Zéphirin (page does not exist)">Frantz Zéphirin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leroy_Exil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leroy Exil (page does not exist)">Leroy Exil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prosper_Pierre_Louis" class="mw-redirect" title="Prosper Pierre Louis">Prosper Pierre Louis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louisiane_Saint_Fleurant" title="Louisiane Saint Fleurant">Louisiane Saint Fleurant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt36_359-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt36-359">[357]</a></sup> Sculpture is also practised in Haiti; noted artists in this form include <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Liautaud&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Liautaud (page does not exist)">George Liautaud</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serge_Jolimeau" title="Serge Jolimeau">Serge Jolimeau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt37_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt37-360">[358]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Haiti" title="Music of Haiti">Music of Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Haitian music combines a wide range of influences drawn from the many people who have settled here. It reflects French, African and Spanish elements and others who have inhabited the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, and minor native <a href="/wiki/Taino" class="mw-redirect" title="Taino">Taino</a> influences. Styles of music unique to the nation of Haiti include music derived from <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Vodou</a> ceremonial traditions, <a href="/wiki/Rara" title="Rara">Rara</a> parading music, <a href="/wiki/Twoubadou" title="Twoubadou">Twoubadou</a> <i>ballads</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mini-jazz" title="Mini-jazz">mini-jazz</a> rock bands, <a href="/wiki/Rasin" title="Rasin">Rasin</a> movement, <a href="/wiki/Haitian_hip_hop" title="Haitian hip hop">Hip hop</a> kreyòl, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9ringue" title="Méringue">méringue</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[359]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Compas" title="Compas">compas</a>. Youth attend parties at nightclubs called <i><a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">discos</a></i>, (pronounced "deece-ko"), and attend <i>Bal</i>. This term is the French word for ball, as in a formal dance. </p>
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Compas" title="Compas">Compas</a> (konpa)</i> (also known as <i>compas direct</i> in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, or <i>konpa dirèk</i> in <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Haitian Creole language">creole</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[360]</a></sup> is a complex, ever-changing music that arose from African rhythms and European ballroom dancing, mixed with Haiti's bourgeois culture. It is a refined music, with <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9ringue" title="Méringue">méringue</a> as its basic rhythm. Haiti had no recorded music until 1937 when <a href="/wiki/Jazz_Guignard" title="Jazz Guignard">Jazz Guignard</a> was recorded non-commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[361]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_literature" title="Haitian literature">Haitian literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Haiti has always been a literary nation that has produced poetry, novels, and plays of international recognition. The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Domingue" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Domingue">French colonial experience</a> established the French language as the venue of culture and prestige, and since then it has dominated the literary circles and the literary production. However, since the 18th century there has been a sustained effort to write in <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>. The recognition of Creole as an official language has led to an expansion of novels, poems, and plays in Creole.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[362]</a></sup> In 1975, <a href="/wiki/Franketienne" class="mw-redirect" title="Franketienne">Franketienne</a> was the first to break with the French tradition in fiction with the publication of <i>Dezafi,</i> the first novel written entirely in Haitian Creole; the work offers a poetic picture of Haitian life.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[363]</a></sup> Other well known Haitian authors include <a href="/wiki/Jean_Price-Mars" title="Jean Price-Mars">Jean Price-Mars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Roumain" title="Jacques Roumain">Jacques Roumain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marie_Vieux-Chauvet" title="Marie Vieux-Chauvet">Marie Vieux-Chauvet</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Clitandre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pierre Clitandre (page does not exist)">Pierre Clitandre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Depestre" title="René Depestre">René Depestre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwidge_Danticat" title="Edwidge Danticat">Edwidge Danticat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyonel_Trouillot" title="Lyonel Trouillot">Lyonel Trouillot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dany_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Dany Laferrière">Dany Laferrière</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3> 
      <p>Haiti has a small though growing cinema industry. Well-known directors working primarily in documentary film-making include <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Peck" title="Raoul Peck">Raoul Peck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Antonin" title="Arnold Antonin">Arnold Antonin</a>. Directors producing fictional films include <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Benoit_(director)" title="Patricia Benoit (director)">Patricia Benoît</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilkenson_Bruna&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wilkenson Bruna (page does not exist)">Wilkenson Bruna</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_Senecal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richard Senecal (page does not exist)">Richard Senecal</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_cuisine" title="Haitian cuisine">Haitian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg/150px-Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="316" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg/225px-Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg/300px-Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1358" data-file-height="2858"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rhum_Barbancourt_Bottle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bottle of Barbancourt Rhum
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Haiti is famous for its <a href="/wiki/Creole_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Creole cuisine">creole cuisine</a> (which related to <a href="/wiki/Cajun_cuisine" title="Cajun cuisine">Cajun cuisine</a>), and its <a href="/wiki/Soup_joumou" title="Soup joumou">soup joumou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[364]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sans-Souci_Palace,_National_History_Park,_Haiti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg/350px-Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg/525px-Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg/700px-Sans-Souci_Palace%2C_National_History_Park%2C_Haiti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4443" data-file-height="2962"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sans-Souci_Palace,_National_History_Park,_Haiti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sans-Souci Palace, National History Park, Haiti
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Haiti" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Haiti">List of World Heritage Sites in Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Monuments include the <a href="/wiki/Sans-Souci_Palace" title="Sans-Souci Palace">Sans-Souci Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Citadelle Laferrière">Citadelle Laferrière</a>, inscribed as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a> in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[365]</a></sup> Situated in the Northern Massif du Nord, in one of Haiti's National Parks, the structures date from the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-heritage_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage-368">[366]</a></sup> The buildings were among the first built after Haiti's independence from France. The <a href="/wiki/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Citadelle Laferrière">Citadelle Laferrière</a>, is the largest fortress in the Americas, is located in northern Haiti. It was built between 1805 and 1820 and is today referred to by some Haitians as the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_wonder_of_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth wonder of the world">eighth wonder of the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reading_Eagle_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reading_Eagle-96">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Institut_de_Sauvegarde_du_Patrimoine_National" title="Institut de Sauvegarde du Patrimoine National">Institute for the Protection of National Heritage</a> has preserved 33 historical monuments and the historic center of Cap-Haïtien.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[367]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">Jacmel</a>, a colonial city that was tentatively accepted as a World Heritage site, was extensively damaged by the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heritage_368-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage-368">[366]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG/170px-Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG/255px-Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG/340px-Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2520" data-file-height="3776"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Maria_Anchor.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Santa María'</i>s anchor on display
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The anchor of Christopher Columbus's largest ship, the <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">Santa María</a></i> now rests in the <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_du_Panth%C3%A9on_National_Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Musée du Panthéon National Haïtien">Musée du Panthéon National Haïtien</a> (MUPANAH), in <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[368]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folklore_and_mythology">Folklore and mythology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_mythology" title="Haitian mythology">Haitian mythology</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Haiti is known for its <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a> traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[369]</a></sup> Much of this is rooted in <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Haitian Vodou</a> tradition. Belief in <a href="/wiki/Zombies" class="mw-redirect" title="Zombies">zombies</a> is also common.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt35_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt35-372">[370]</a></sup> Other folkloric creatures include the <a href="/wiki/Soucouyant" title="Soucouyant">lougarou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradt35_372-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradt35-372">[370]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_holidays_and_festivals">National holidays and festivals</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Haiti" title="Public holidays in Haiti">Public holidays in Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most festive time of the year in Haiti is during <i><b><a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a></b></i> (referred to as <i>Kanaval</i> in <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras" title="Mardi Gras">Mardi Gras</a>) in February.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="need to justify">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There is music, parade floats, and dancing and singing in the streets. Carnival week is traditionally a time of all-night parties. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rara" title="Rara">Rara</a> is a festival celebrated before <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a>. The festival has generated a style of <a href="/wiki/Carnival_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Carnival music">Carnival music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[371]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[372]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg/220px-Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg/330px-Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg/440px-Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1923" data-file-height="1241"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Haiti_national_football_team_training_in_Port-au-Prince_2004-08-16_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Haiti_national_football_team" title="Haiti national football team">Haiti national football team</a> training in Port-au-Prince, 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (soccer) is the most popular sport in Haiti with hundreds of small football clubs competing at the local level. Basketball is growing in popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-375">[373]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stade_Sylvio_Cator" title="Stade Sylvio Cator">Stade Sylvio Cator</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium" title="Multi-purpose stadium">multi-purpose stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, where it is currently used mostly for <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> matches that fits a capacity of 10,000 people. In <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Haiti_national_football_team" title="Haiti national football team">Haiti national football team</a> were only the second <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> team to make the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>'s entry in 1938). They lost in the opening qualifying stages against three of the pre-tournament favorites; <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>. The national team won the <a href="/wiki/2007_Caribbean_Nations_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Caribbean Nations Cup">2007 Caribbean Nations Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[374]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Haiti has participated in the <a href="/wiki/Haiti_at_the_Olympics" title="Haiti at the Olympics">Olympic Games</a> since the year 1900 and won a number of medals. Haitian footballer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Gaetjens" title="Joe Gaetjens">Joe Gaetjens</a> played for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States national team</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950 FIFA World Cup</a>, scoring the winning goal in the 1–0 upset of <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[375]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_natives_and_residents">Notable natives and residents</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Haitians" title="List of Haitians">List of Haitians</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:WyclefJean.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/WyclefJean.jpg/170px-WyclefJean.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/WyclefJean.jpg/255px-WyclefJean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/WyclefJean.jpg/340px-WyclefJean.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:WyclefJean.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Hector,_comte_d%27Estaing" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Hector, comte d'Estaing">Comte d'Estaing</a>&nbsp;– in command of more than 500 volunteers from Saint-Domingue; fought alongside American colonial troops against the British in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Savannah" title="Siege of Savannah">Siege of Savannah</a>, one of the most significant foreign contributions to the American Revolutionary War in 1779<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[376]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Raquel_Pelissier" class="mw-redirect" title="Raquel Pelissier">Raquel Pelissier</a>&nbsp;– one of Haiti's most remarkable beauty queen; <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe_2017" title="Miss Universe 2017">Miss Universe 2017</a> first runner-up and <a href="/wiki/Reina_Hispanoamericana" title="Reina Hispanoamericana">Reina Hispanoamericana</a> 2016 third runner-up</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Frank%C3%A9tienne" title="Frankétienne">Frankétienne</a>&nbsp;– arguably Haiti's greatest author; candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 2009</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Garcelle_Beauvais" title="Garcelle Beauvais">Garcelle Beauvais</a>&nbsp;– television actress (<i><a href="/wiki/NYPD_Blue" title="NYPD Blue">NYPD Blue</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jamie_Foxx_Show" title="The Jamie Foxx Show">The Jamie Foxx Show</a></i>)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Point_du_Sable" title="Jean Baptiste Point du Sable">Jean Baptiste Point du Sable</a>&nbsp;– might have been born in St Marc, Saint-Domingue; in 1745 established a <a href="/wiki/Fur_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Fur trading">fur trading</a> post at present-day Chicago, Illinois; considered one of the city's founders</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte" title="Jean Lafitte">Jean Lafitte</a>&nbsp;– pirate who operated around <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Coast">Gulf Coast</a> of the United States; born in Port-au-Prince around 1782<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[377]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/John_James_Audubon" title="John James Audubon">John James Audubon</a>&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Ornithologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ornithologist">ornithologist</a> and painter; born in 1785 in Les Cayes, Saint-Domingue; his parents returned to France, where he was educated; emigrated to the United States as a young man and made a career as he painted, catalogued and described the birds of North America</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B8rgen_Leth" title="Jørgen Leth">Jørgen Leth</a>&nbsp;– Danish poet and filmmaker<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[378]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a> – American <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscar Award">Oscar Award</a>-winning actor, who currently serves as <i>Ambassador-at-large</i> for Haiti; the first non-Haitian citizen to hold such a position<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[379]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Micha%C3%ABlle_Jean" title="Michaëlle Jean">Michaëlle Jean</a>&nbsp;– current <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Secretary-General of La Francophonie</a> and 27th <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>; born in Port-au-Prince in 1957 and lived in Haiti until 1968</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>-winning hip-hop recording artist</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Haiti" title="Education in Haiti">Education in Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Universite_henrichristophe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Universite_henrichristophe.jpg/220px-Universite_henrichristophe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Universite_henrichristophe.jpg/330px-Universite_henrichristophe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Universite_henrichristophe.jpg/440px-Universite_henrichristophe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Universite_henrichristophe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Universite Roi Henri Christophe in <a href="/wiki/Limonade" title="Limonade">Limonade</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The educational system of Haiti is based on the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_France" title="Education in France">French system</a>. Higher education, under the responsibility of the Ministry of Education,<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[380]</a></sup> is provided by universities and other public and private institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[381]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than 80% of primary schools are privately managed by nongovernmental organizations, churches, communities, and for-profit operators, with minimal government oversight.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[382]</a></sup> According to the 2013 Millennium Development Goals (MDG) Report, Haiti has steadily boosted net enrollment rate in primary education from 47% in 1993 to 88% in 2011, achieving equal participation of boys and girls in education.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[383]</a></sup> Charity organizations, including <a href="/wiki/Food_for_the_Poor" title="Food for the Poor">Food for the Poor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Health_Foundation" title="Haitian Health Foundation">Haitian Health Foundation</a>, are building schools for children and providing necessary school supplies. According to CIA 2015 <a href="/wiki/World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a>, Haiti's literacy rate is now 60.7% (est. 2015). </p>
      <p>The January 2010 earthquake, was a major setback for education reform in Haiti as it diverted limited resources to survival.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[384]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many reformers have advocated the creation of a free, public and universal education system for all primary school-age students in Haiti. The <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a> estimates that the government will need at least US$3 billion to create an adequately funded system.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[385]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Upon successful graduation of secondary school, students may continue into <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>. The higher education schools in Haiti include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Haiti" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Haiti">University of Haiti</a>. There are also <a href="/wiki/List_of_medical_schools_in_the_Caribbean" title="List of medical schools in the Caribbean">medical schools</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legal_education" title="Legal education">law schools</a> offered at both the University of Haiti and abroad. Presently, <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> is cooperating with L'Hôpital Saint-Damien in Haiti to coordinate a <a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">pediatric health care</a> curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[386]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Haiti" title="Health in Haiti">Health in Haiti</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the past, children's vaccination rates have been low&nbsp;– as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 60% of the children in Haiti under the age of 10 were <a href="/wiki/Vaccine" title="Vaccine">vaccinated</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[387]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[388]</a></sup> compared to rates of childhood vaccination in other countries in the 93–95% range.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[389]</a></sup> Recently there have been mass vaccination campaigns claiming to vaccinate as many as 91% of a target population against specific diseases (measles and rubella in this case).<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[390]</a></sup> Most people have no transportation or access to <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Haiti" title="List of hospitals in Haiti">Haitian hospitals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[391]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> cites <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrheal</a> diseases, <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a>, and respiratory infections as common causes of death in Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[392]</a></sup> Ninety percent of Haiti's children suffer from <a href="/wiki/Waterborne_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterborne disease">waterborne diseases</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intestinal_parasite" class="mw-redirect" title="Intestinal parasite">intestinal parasites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">[393]</a></sup> HIV infection is found in 1.71% of Haiti's population (est. 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[394]</a></sup> The incidence of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> (TB) in Haiti is more than ten times as high as in the rest of Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[395]</a></sup> Approximately 30,000 Haitians fall ill with <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> each year.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">[396]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most people living in Haiti are at high risk for major infectious diseases. Food or <a href="/wiki/Waterborne_diseases" title="Waterborne diseases">water-borne</a> diseases include bacterial and protozoal <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">hepatitis</a> A and E; common <a href="/wiki/Vector_(epidemiology)" title="Vector (epidemiology)">vector</a>-borne diseases are <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>; water-contact diseases include <a href="/wiki/Leptospirosis" title="Leptospirosis">leptospirosis</a>. Roughly 75% of Haitian households lack running water. Unsafe water, along with inadequate housing and unsanitary living conditions, contributes to the high incidence of infectious diseases. There is a chronic shortage of health care personnel and hospitals lack resources, a situation that became readily apparent after the January 2010 earthquake.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[397]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> in Haiti in 2013 was 55 deaths per 1,000 live births, compared to a rate of 6 per 1,000 in other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[398]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the 2010 earthquake, <a href="/wiki/Partners_In_Health" title="Partners In Health">Partners In Health</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4pital_Universitaire_de_Mirebalais" title="Hôpital Universitaire de Mirebalais">Hôpital Universitaire de Mirebalais</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar-powered</a> hospital in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[399]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">[400]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <ol class="references"> 
        <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The nation was officially founded as <i>Hayti</i> in its Declaration of Independence (and early prints),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> constitutions,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and imperial declarations.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Published writings of 1802–1919 in the United States commonly used the name "Hayti" (e.g. <i>The Blue Book of Hayti</i> (1919), a book with official standing in Haiti). By 1873 "Haiti" was common among titles of US published books as well as in US congressional publications. In all of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>' publications after 1890, he used "Haiti". As late as 1949, the name "Hayti" continued to be used in books published in England (e.g. <i>Hayti: 145 Years of Independence—The Bi-Centenary of Port-au-Prince</i> published in London, England in 1949) but by 1950, usage in England had shifted to "Haiti".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Taínos may have used <i>Bohío</i> as another name for the island.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></span> </li> 
       </ol>
      </div>
